                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex"> ${D}_{{\text{Na}}^{+}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> throughout the charge/discharge processes, as well as the same values between the fourth cycle and first cycle, also suggests a solid-solution pathway and a stable structure.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2565-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cbb8136f-bf5b-4217-9a43-cdaa00231462/cey2565-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/cbb8136f-bf5b-4217-9a43-cdaa00231462/cey2565-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3d2cfc58-af5c-4737-878f-163e70bbf64b/cey2565-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cbb8136f-bf5b-4217-9a43-cdaa00231462/cey2565-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2565-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.565" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A) CV curves and (B) capacity contribution ratios at various scan rates from 0.1 to 1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, (C) capacitive current separated from total current at 0.4 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, (D) GITT curves,&nbsp;(E) corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity versus state of charge and discharge at 0.1 C, (F) in&nbsp;situ EIS test procedure, (G) fitting results, and (H) changes of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>CEI</sub> of O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In situ, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was collected for the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode at given voltages from the open-circuit voltage (OCV) to charge states of 4.3 V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2565-fig-0004">4F,G</a>). Based on an equivalent circuit model, clearly, all Nyquist plots consist of three parts separated by frequency: an intercept with the abscissa corresponding to the ohmic resistance (<i>R</i><sub>s</sub> or <i>R</i><sub>1</sub>) in the high frequency, two semicircles reflecting the interface contact impendence (<i>R</i><sub>CEI</sub> or <i>R</i><sub>2</sub>), and charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> or <i>R</i><sub>3</sub>) in the middle frequency, as well as a short slopping tail reflecting Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion at low frequency. Compared with <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and R<sub>CEI</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> can be ignored as it is only 4–6 Ω and remains unchanged. The fitted impedance values of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and R<sub>CEI</sub> are summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>&nbsp;and change tendencies are shown in Figure <a href="#cey2565-fig-0004">4H</a>. Impressively, both <i>R</i><sub>CEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> decrease sharply as the cell is charged to 3.2 V from the maximum values at the OCV state, suggesting that the phase transition from O3 to P3 at low voltage allows the host to provide wider channels and larger layer spacing for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. Although the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> changes obviously with the Na<sup>+</sup> extraction, the <i>R</i><sub>CEI</sub> maintains unchanged even when the cell is charged to 4.3 V, indicating that the CEI formed on the surface of the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 particle is very stable and robust, as observed by the SEM. All of these findings should be attributed to the stable crystal structure of the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode upon the effectively inhibited phase transition of P3–O′3 at high voltage. Additionally, the stabilized CEI continuously protects the TM cations from dissolution in the electrolyte and ensures fast Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics.</p>
         
         <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2565-fig-0005">5A,D</a> schematically illustrates the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion pathways along the Na layer in the crystal models of P2/O3-NaNMFT and O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathodes based on density functional theory (DFT) structural calculations. Combined with the climbing image nudged elastic band (CI-NEB) method, the migration energy barrier of interspecies of O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 model upon Na<sup>+</sup> extraction was determined to be 612 meV, which is smaller than 628 meV of the P2/O3-NaNMFT model without Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2565-fig-0005">5B,E</a>). The decreased diffusion barrier is likely due to the fact that Li<sup>+</sup> has a larger ionic radius than MT cations (Ni<sup>2+</sup>, Mn<sup>4+</sup>), leading to a weaker Coulomb repulsive interaction between the diffusing Na<sup>+</sup> and the underneath metal cations along the investigated migration pathway. Such a mechanism promotes the electrochemical reaction at a high rate and maintains the thermodynamically stable phase throughout the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion process. Valence charge density distribution and charge density difference between O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 and P2/O3-NaNMFT cathodes were analyzed to reveal the effects of Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution (highlighted by the red circle) on the charge transfer and charge density distribution of the crystal models (Figure <a href="#cey2565-fig-0005">5C,F</a>). Different from the TM–O bonds in both P2/O3-NaNMFT and O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 models, which are strong polar covalent bonds, Li–O bonds in the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 model exhibit mainly ionic character. In addition, all Na–O bonds remain ionic in both models. As shown in Figure <a href="#cey2565-fig-0005">5F</a>, the nearby MT atoms lose more valence electrons to the surrounding O atoms due to the obvious univalent state of Li<sup>+</sup>. Notably, the blue and yellow areas around the TM and O atoms indicate that the charge transfer between&nbsp;TM–O bonds is more pronounced in the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 model. Combined with the highly ionized Li<sup>+</sup> being easy to insert/extract from the lattice and the stronger interaction of MT atoms with O (TM–O) after Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution, as predicted, the Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution effectively improves the thermodynamic stability and electrochemical reaction kinetics as well as the structural stability. Because different from the complex transition (P2/O3–P2/O3/P3–P2/P3–P2/Z/O3′–Z/O3′) in the P2/O3-NaNMFT cathode, the P3–O3′ phase transition is successfully mitigated at high voltage in O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode with a only structural evolution of O3–P3 (Figure <a href="#cey2565-fig-0005">5G</a>). Hence, such a stable structure cathode is beneficial to high-voltage electrochemical energy storage.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2565-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/919c974e-5700-4435-a95c-ba0fcfc77839/cey2565-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/919c974e-5700-4435-a95c-ba0fcfc77839/cey2565-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/efd41f0a-a24b-4508-a7e7-45dcf9c64c7a/cey2565-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/919c974e-5700-4435-a95c-ba0fcfc77839/cey2565-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2565-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.565" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A, D) Schematic Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion pathway. (B, E) Activation barrier energy, and (C) charge density distribution for NaNMFT and NaLNMFT. (F) Quadratic difference calculation based on O3-NaLNMFT–P2/O3-NaNMFT and (G) schematic diagram of the phase transition process in P2/O3-NaNMFT and O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 during the charging process.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2565-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2565-sec-0030-title">3 CONCLUSION</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, rational thermodynamically crystallographic evolution&nbsp;from P2/O3 biphase to O3 monophase in NaLNMFT-<i>x</i> cathode system induced by Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution for Ni<sup>2+</sup> was reported for SIBs. The efficient Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution not only simplified the electrochemical high-voltage phase transition of P3–O3′ but also promoted a robust CEI to block the loss of TM ions of the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode upon repeated Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion. Moreover, DFT calculations and kinetic analysis revealed that the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 model showed both a reduced energy barrier of 612 meV and a high Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of 1.1 × 10<sup>−11</sup>–3.07 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> due to the changed local coordination of TMO<sub>2</sub> slabs. As a result, the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06 cathode exhibited excellent cycling stability for Na<sup>+</sup> storage with capacity retentions of 89.6% (116.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 1 C) after 200 cycles and 81.6% (97.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, 5 C) after 500 cycles. Moreover, the O3-NaLNMFT-0.06//HC full cell demonstrated a promising energy density (285 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup>) with a retention of 80.1%. Such exceptional electrochemical performance highlights&nbsp;O3-NaLNMFT as a promising cathode candidate of SIBs and provides new insights for the future long life and practical material design for energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2565-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2565-sec-0040-title">4 EXPERIMENTAL SECTION</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2565-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2565-sec-0050-title">4.1 Materials preparation</h3>
            
            <p>The targeted cathode materials were prepared by using conventional solid-state reaction as the formula of Na<sub>0.766+<i>x</i></sub>Li<sub><i>x</i></sub>Ni<sub>0.33−<i>x</i></sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.07</sub>O<sub>2</sub> by using Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, NiO, MnO<sub>2</sub>, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, and TiO<sub>2</sub> as raw materials, which all were purchased from Aladdin company. Simply, the stoichiometrically mixed raw materials were grounded, pressed into pellets at 16 MPa, and annealed at 950°C under air for 15 h, followed by cooling them&nbsp;down to room temperature. Six composites are uniformly abbreviated as NaLNMFT-0.02, -0.04, -0.06, -0.08, and -0.1 based on the amount of Li<sup>+&nbsp;</sup>substitution (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2565-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2565-sec-0060-title">4.2 Material characterization</h3>
            
            <p>XRD patterns were collected on a Bruker D8 diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation (<i>λ</i> = 1.5418 Å) in a scanning range (2<i>θ</i>) of 10°–80° with a sweep speed of 2° min<sup>–1</sup>. The data were refined by using TOPAS software to acquire the crystallographic parameters. SEM and HRTEM images were, respectively, collected using JEOL (JSM-6390LA) and FEI (Tecnai G2 F20) equipment. Both the HAADF and ABF images were captured using an&nbsp;aberration-corrected&nbsp;STEM at 200 kV (JEOL ARM200F). TOF-SIMS measurement was performed on an ION-TOF M6 instrument. The ex situ Ni and Fe K-edge XAS spectra were recorded in fluorescence mode at beamline BL13SSW of the Shanghai Synchrotron Radiation Facility.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2565-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2565-sec-0070-title">4.3 Electrochemical characterizations</h3>
            
            <p>All electrochemical performances were carried out on CR2032-type coin half-cells, which were assembled in argon-filled glove boxes (&lt;0.2 ppm of H<sub>2</sub>O and O<sub>2</sub>) with Na foil as the anode, NaLNMFT as the cathodes, porous glass fiber as the separator, and 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in propyl carbonate&nbsp;with 5 vol% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) as the electrolyte. To get the cathodes, slurries were prepared at first by hybridizing active materials, a conductive agent of super P, and a binder of polyvinylidene fluoride&nbsp;with a mass ratio of 8:1:1 in <i>N</i>-methyl-pyrrolidinone, respectively. Then, the cathodes were obtained by coating as-prepared slurries on Al foil using a doctor blade followed by&nbsp;drying overnight under a vacuum with an average mass loading of 1.5–2.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The GCD&nbsp;and CV&nbsp;tests were performed on a Land BT2000 battery system and an electrochemical workstation (Autolab M204) with a voltage potential of 2.2–4.3 V (vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at room temperature. In situ, EIS&nbsp;tests were performed at the given potentials of the first charge process after holding at OCV for 1 h to reach the stable state. The frequency is set in the range of 10 MHz–100 KHz, and the test potential amplitude is 5 mV. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients were acquired via the GITT&nbsp;test in the cell repeated at 0.1 C for 30 min and then relaxed for 10 h within the whole process. HC was assembled as the anode in the full cell tests, and the mass ratio between the cathode and anode is 1.05:1.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2565-sec-0080">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2565-sec-0080-title">4.4 DFT calculation</h3>
            
            <p>First-principles computations were carried out by using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package (VASP.5.4.4).<span><sup><a href="#cey2565-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2565-bib-0043_R_d29332205e1932" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J Comput Chem">43</a></sup></span> The valence electron orbitals of relevant atoms were treated by the projector augmented wave&nbsp;method. The NEB&nbsp;method was employed to calculate the migration energy profile for Na<sup>+</sup> on each diffusion pathway.<span><sup><a href="#cey2565-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2565-bib-0044_R_d29332205e1937" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Phys Rev B">44</a>, <a href="#cey2565-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2565-bib-0045_R_d29332205e1937" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - J Appl Crystal">45</a></sup></span> The charge density and bond lengths of TM–O and Na–O were calculated and visualized by Visualization for Electronic and Structure Analysis. The van der Waals interactions played a negligible role in the investigated structures since the chemical interactions were mainly ionic and polar covalent bonds among constituting atoms. According to the experimental composition, three modeling structures were built, P2-Na<sub>18</sub>Ti<sub>1</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>Ni<sub>6</sub>Mn<sub>9</sub>O<sub>36</sub>, O3-Na<sub>27</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>Ni<sub>9</sub>Mn<sub>13</sub>O<sub>54</sub>, and O3-Na<sub>27</sub>Li<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>Ni<sub>7</sub>Mn<sub>13</sub>O<sub>54</sub>. In the O3 structure, Li, Ni, Mn, Fe, and Ti atoms occupying 3b Wyckoff sites were randomly placed in the MO<sub>6</sub> layers, and all Na atoms were assigned to the 3a Wyckoff sites. Similarly, the Ni, Mn, Fe, and Ti atoms occupying 2a Wyckoff sites in the P2 structure were randomly placed in the MO<sub>6</sub> layers. It is worth noting that the irreversible Na ordering in the structure optimization process will have a certain impact on the accuracy of the diffusion barrier calculation, so the Na species in three modeled structures were completely occupied and assigned to 2b Wyckoff sites. Finally, the 3 × 3 × 1 supercell models of Na<sub>18</sub>Ti<sub>1</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>Ni<sub>6</sub>Mn<sub>9</sub>O<sub>36</sub>, Na<sub>27</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>Ni<sub>9</sub>Mn<sub>13</sub>O<sub>54</sub>, and Na<sub>27</sub>Li<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>Ni<sub>7</sub>Mn<sub>13</sub>O<sub>54</sub> were obtained based on the original cell of P2/O3 Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> phase and the Rietveld refinement results. The kinetic energy cutoff value was set to 500 eV for plane wave expansion in reciprocal space. Due to the use of large supercells, the energy integration in the first Brillouin zone was conducted using a single <i>k</i> point at <i>Γ</i>-point. The convergence thresholds were set to 10<sup>−6</sup> eV for total energy and 0.05 eV Å<sup>−1</sup> for the atomic force, respectively.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
